‚óŹ Everything in one ‚ÄĒ understood. I'll honor that, but I'll structure it so the
  implementation is many independent, individually-testable pieces (one profile
  = one task) even though it's a single spec. Here's the full design.

  Generalized extraction via platform profiles ‚ÄĒ design

  1. Architecture. Extract the Commvault-specific TOC discovery and
  content-scoping out of FirecrawlService into a profile abstraction. A profile
  implements:
  - detect(root_html) -> confidence ‚ÄĒ fingerprint match.
  - build_toc(root_url, scraper) -> list[TocEntry] ‚ÄĒ returns ordered entries
  with (title, url, level, parent).
  - content_config(url) -> {includeTags?, onlyMainContent?, waitFor?} ‚ÄĒ per-page
  scrape options.

  FirecrawlService becomes profile-agnostic: pick profile ‚Üí build_toc (Phase 1)
  ‚Üí per-page scrape using content_config (Phase 2). All existing infra (worker
  queue, changeTracking, images, incremental, removed-page detection) is
  untouched ‚ÄĒ profiles only change how the TOC is built and which DOM is 
  content.

  2. Selection. New DocumentationSource.platform field (+ optional
  profile_config JSON for overrides/derived selectors). On first run (or on
  demand), a detector fingerprints the rendered root HTML and sets platform; the
  UI shows a dropdown (known platforms + Auto + Generic). User override always
  wins.

  3. Profile catalog (the 5 strategies, covering all surveyed targets):

  Profile: Commvault
  Strategy: sidebar-tree
  TOC build: #nav .nav-group recursive (existing)
  Content: #doc
  Risk: low (done)
  ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ

  Content: .theme-doc-markdown/article
  Risk: low

  ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ
  Profile: MadCap Flare WebHelp
  Strategy: frames/topic-files
  TOC build: Flare TOC data (Data/Toc*) or topic enumeration
  Content: topic page body (not the frameset)
  Risk: high (frames)
  ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ

  ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ
  Profile: Freshdesk help center

  TOC build: /support/solutions categories‚Üífolders‚Üíarticles

  ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ
  Profile: Confluence
  Strategy: sidebar-tree (JS)
  TOC build: rendered space page-tree (waitFor)
  Content: .wiki-content
  Risk: highest (JS-gated; may need Firecrawl actions; API is the documented
    escape hatch if DOM proves too fragile)
  ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ
  Profile: Generic fallback
  Strategy: sitemap+URL-path
  TOC build: sitemap.xml / Firecrawl /map ‚Üí hierarchy from URL paths
  Content: onlyMainContent
  Risk: ordering best-effort
  ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ
  Profile: LLM fallback
  Strategy: derived
  TOC build: LLM inspects rendered root (+1 child) ‚Üí classifies strategy + emits

    nav/content/parent selectors ‚Üí cached as profile_config, then run
    deterministically
  Content: per derived selectors
  Risk: bounded, one-shot/source

  4. Ordering guarantee. Sidebar/tree/hub-spoke/Flare strategies preserve source
  order naturally (DOM/crawl order). Only the generic sitemap fallback can't
  preserve true TOC order (sitemaps are flat) ‚ÄĒ there it's best-effort (URL-path
  grouping). This keeps the tool's "preserve original TOC order" promise for
  every recognized platform.

  5. Testing. The many profiles are made testable with saved HTML fixtures (the
  real pages I scraped during this survey become
  tests/fixtures/platforms/*.html): detect() and build_toc() are unit-tested
  offline against fixtures (deterministic, no network), so each profile has real
  coverage. Plus a per-platform live smoke check during verification (scrape
  the real root, assert a sane ordered TOC + non-empty content). The LLM
  fallback is tested with a mocked LLM returning a fixed profile_config.

  6. Out of scope / risks I'm flagging: Confluence under pure-scraping is the
  riskiest (heavy JS) ‚ÄĒ if its rendered tree proves unreliable, the fallback is
  its REST API as a follow-on. The LLM fallback adds a model dependency + cost;
  it's a safety net, not the common path.

  Does this shape look right ‚ÄĒ the profile interface, the catalog/strategies,
  auto-detect+override, fixture-based testing, and the Confluence/LLM risk
  flags? If so I'll write the spec.

  grinding all 13 inline in one stretch is slower and lower-quality, and the two
  risk profiles really want a live-data loop.

‚úĽ Worked for 10m 58s

‚ĚĮ How does the LLM fallback work?                                               

‚óŹ Let me read the actual implementation so I describe it accurately rather than
  from memory.
  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

‚óŹ Here's how the LLM fallback works, end to end.

  Where it sits ‚ÄĒ last resort, opt-in

  The resolver (FirecrawlService._resolve_profile) picks a profile in this
  order:
  1. Stored source.platform override (your UI dropdown)
  2. Fingerprint auto-detect ‚ÄĒ the 11 deterministic profiles' detect() against
  the rendered root
  3. LLM fallback ‚ÄĒ only if settings.llm_fallback_enabled is True
  (DOCEXTRACTOR_LLM_FALLBACK_ENABLED, default off)
  4. Generic sitemap fallback

  So the LLM never fires for any site a real profile recognizes. Its detect()
  always returns False ‚ÄĒ it's never auto-selected; it's only reachable as an
  explicit, enabled step between auto-detect and generic. With the flag off (the
  default), build_toc returns [] immediately and the chain falls through to
  generic ‚ÄĒ zero behavior change and zero cost for everyone.

  What it does when enabled

  For an unrecognized site (build_toc, lines 148‚Äď187):
  1. Scrape the root HTML via the same Scraper adapter the other profiles use.
  2. Send the first 20 000 chars of that HTML + the URL to Claude Haiku 4.5
  (claude-haiku-4-5) with a system prompt asking it to classify the site and
  return only JSON:
  { "strategy": "sidebar|hubspoke|sitemap",
    "nav_selector": "...",            // sidebar
    "category_link_selector": "...",  // hubspoke
    "article_link_selector": "...",   // hubspoke
    "content_selector": "..." }       // optional
  3. Dispatch to the same shared strategy helpers the deterministic profiles
  use, with the LLM's selectors:
    - sidebar ‚Üí sidebar_tree_toc(scraper, root_url, nav_selector)
    - hubspoke ‚Üí hubspoke_toc(..., category/article selectors)
    - sitemap/unknown ‚Üí sitemap_urls(...) as a flat best-effort list

  The key idea: the LLM only picks the strategy + CSS selectors; the proven 
  extraction code does the actual TOC building. The model isn't parsing the
  whole doc ‚ÄĒ it's a narrow classifier that adapts our existing machinery to an
  unknown DOM.

  Design choices worth knowing

  - Injectable client (__init__(self, client=None)): the profile takes a
  callable (html, root_url) ‚Üí spec. Tests inject a fake spec; the real Anthropic
  HTTP path (_build_default_client, lines 75‚Äď116) is built lazily and only ever
  runs when the flag is on and anthropic_api_key is set. That's why it's fully
  unit-tested without ever calling a model.
  - Resilient: the whole thing is wrapped in try/except ‚Üí [] (line¬†183) ‚ÄĒ a bad
  LLM response, malformed JSON, missing key, or network error never crashes an
  extraction; it just degrades to the generic fallback.

  Current limitations (documented follow-ons, lines 29‚Äď40)

  1. No per-source caching. The profile interface doesn't pass the source into
  build_toc, so the derived spec can't be persisted to source.profile_config ‚ÄĒ
  meaning each run re-calls the LLM. The fix is to add a source hook to the
  interface and cache the spec.
  2. Content uses the generic heuristic. content_config() returns
  {"onlyMainContent": True} rather than the LLM's content_selector, because that
  selector can't be threaded through without the caching above.
  3. Sync httpx in an async path (flagged in review) ‚ÄĒ the default client uses
  blocking httpx.post, which would stall the worker's event loop if enabled; a
  follow-on should switch to httpx.AsyncClient.

  Bottom line: it's a deliberately narrow, gated safety net ‚ÄĒ an LLM picks a
  strategy + selectors for genuinely unknown sites, and our deterministic
  helpers do the extraction. It's off by default, and since all 12 of your real
  targets fingerprint cleanly, nothing currently needs it.

  - Settings (generalize): llm_fallback_enabled (keep), llm_provider

  ‚ÄĒ build_toc dispatches by strategy; content_config uses the spec's
  content_selector when present (content-aware), else onlyMainContent.

  source.profile_config["llm_spec"] if cached (no LLM call), else derive once
  (reusing the root HTML already scraped for detection) and persist the spec ‚Üí
  return DerivedProfile. This is the "source hook + cache" without changing the
  profile interface (the spec rides on a per-source instance).

‚óŹ Done ‚ÄĒ all three enhancements shipped, reviewed, and pushed to PR #5 (commit
  97e1f6d, 294 tests passing).

  What changed

  1. Spec caching + content-awareness (the "source hook")
  The resolver now caches the LLM-derived spec to
  source.profile_config["llm_spec"] and reuses it on every subsequent run with 
  no LLM call. Implemented without changing the profile interface: a
  DerivedProfile(spec) is built per-source and carries the spec, so its
  content_config() returns the LLM's content_selector as includeTags (content
  capture is now spec-aware) instead of the generic onlyMainContent heuristic.
  The review specifically verified the persistence is correct ‚ÄĒ it's a new-dict 
  assignment so SQLAlchemy's JSONB change-tracking actually saves it, and a
  call-counter test proves the second resolve doesn't re-derive.

  2. httpx.AsyncClient
  derive_spec is now fully async ‚ÄĒ no more blocking the worker's event loop.

  3. Provider-agnostic
  New settings replace the Anthropic-only key:

  What shipped

  1. Dropdown options ‚ÄĒ PLATFORM_OPTIONS now includes Salesforce (among the
  named platforms) and LLM fallback (at the end), so all 12 profiles + Auto +
  Generic are selectable. Selecting llm triggers the resolver's explicit-LLM

  2. "Re-derive" action ‚ÄĒ a per-row button that PATCHes refresh_profile: true,
  which clears the cached profile_config.llm_spec:
  - Backend drops only the llm_spec key (retaining any other profile_config
  data) via a new-dict assignment so SQLAlchemy's JSONB change-tracking actually
  persists it, and it's a safe no-op when there's no cached spec. Covered by 3
  new async route tests (asserting against the DB row directly).
  - Frontend button stops row-click propagation, calls updateSource, and
  refreshes via the existing callback.

  The next extraction after a re-derive rebuilds the DerivedProfile(spec) from
  scratch ‚ÄĒ exactly your "something changed in the source" case ‚ÄĒ while normal
  runs keep using the cache.

  Two minor review notes I left as-is (both harmless, your call): the new button
  sits inside the same <label> that already wrapped the platform <select>
  (non-conforming HTML but browsers handle it), and the button shows on every
  row including non-LLM ones (hiding it conditionally would mean exposing
  profile_config to the frontend).

  One thing I must pin down on storage, because it changes the topology: VMware 
  CSI does RWO block volumes by default; ReadWriteMany needs vSAN File volumes
  specifically. Since exports/ + media/ are written by the worker and served by
  the backend, they need the same volume.

‚óŹ¬†User answered Claude's questions:
  ‚éŅ ¬†¬∑ Does your VMware CSI StorageClass support ReadWriteMany (RWX) volumes 
     (i.e. vSAN File Services), or only ReadWriteOnce (RWX) block volumes? This 
     decides how backend + worker share exports/media. ‚Üí RWO block only

‚óŹ RWO block only ‚Üí backend and worker must co-locate on one node and share RWO
  PVCs (RWO = one node, so multiple pods on that node can both mount), each
  pinned to 1 replica via podAffinity. That's the key topology constraint. Let
  me confirm one app detail (a health endpoint for probes) before presenting the
  design.

  Ran 1 shell command (ctrl+o to expand)

‚óŹ All facts gathered (and there's already a /api/health endpoint for probes).
  Here's the design.

  Kubernetes deployment ‚ÄĒ design

  Deliverable & layout. A single Helm umbrella chart at
  deploy/helm/docextractor/ (source of truth), plus a committed helm 
  template-rendered plain-manifest set under deploy/rendered/ so "manifests"
  exist for non-Helm use. A values.yaml (documented defaults) and a concrete
  values-homelab.yaml (ghcr images, RWO storage class, host
  docextractor.k3s.home.lan).

  Components & topology (translating the 5 compose services).
  - postgres ‚ÄĒ StatefulSet + headless Service + RWO PVC (volumeClaimTemplate),
  gated by postgres.enabled (off ‚Üí use externalDatabaseUrl). Creds from Secret.
  - backend (web) ‚ÄĒ Deployment replicas:1, ClusterIP Service :8000, mounts the
  shared exports + media RWO PVCs. Probes on /api/health.
  - worker (python -m app.worker) ‚ÄĒ Deployment replicas:1, podAffinity 
  co-locating it with the backend pod so both land on the same node and can
  share the RWO exports/media PVCs (RWO = one node, multiple pods OK).
  - scheduler (python -m app.scheduler) ‚ÄĒ Deployment replicas:1, no volumes.
  - frontend ‚ÄĒ Deployment + ClusterIP Service :80 + Traefik Ingress (host
  docextractor.k3s.home.lan, HTTP; tls values-toggle for later). Its nginx.conf
  moves into a templated ConfigMap so proxy_pass targets the backend Service DNS
  (keeping the existing single-origin model: /api + /media proxied to the
  backend, SPA fallback).

  ‚Ėé Scaling caveat (documented): backend+worker are pinned to 1 replica and 
  ‚Ėé co-located because of RWO. Independent horizontal scaling needs RWX (vSAN 
  ‚Ėé File / Longhorn / NFS) later ‚ÄĒ at which point it's just a values change 
  ‚Ėé (accessMode RWX, drop the affinity).

  Networking / webhook. DOCEXTRACTOR_WEBHOOK_BASE_URL becomes the in-cluster
  backend Service DNS (http://<release>-backend.<ns>.svc.cluster.local:8000) ‚ÄĒ
  Firecrawl runs in the same k3s cluster, so it reaches the backend Service
  directly (the compose host-IP hack disappears).

  Config & secrets. ConfigMap for non-secret env (Firecrawl URL, webhook base,
  CORS host, LLM provider/model/base_url). Secret for DB password,
  FIRECRAWL_API_KEY, LLM_API_KEY. The async+sync DB URLs are composed from the
  postgres Service + secret. Plain k8s Secret driven by values (swappable for
  sealed-secrets later ‚ÄĒ noted, not built).

  Migrations. A Helm pre-install/pre-upgrade hook Job runs alembic upgrade head
  once per deploy (backend image + DB secret). The backend Dockerfile CMD drops
  to just uvicorn (the inline alembic && uvicorn becomes the Job) ‚ÄĒ exactly what
  the Dockerfile comment already anticipates.

  Images & CI. Images at ghcr.io/carev01/doc-extractor-{backend,frontend}. I'll
  add a GitHub Actions workflow that builds + pushes both on push to main and on
  version tags (tagged latest + git-sha/tag). Since the repo will be public,
  ghcr packages are anonymously pullable (no imagePullSecret); an
  imagePullSecret values block is included but default-off.

  Probes/resources. backend+frontend HTTP readiness/liveness (/api/health, /);
  postgres pg_isready; worker/scheduler lightweight liveness (exec); modest
  CPU/mem requests+limits in values.

  Validation/testing. helm lint, helm template rendering, and schema-validation
  of the rendered output (kubeconform / kubectl --dry-run=client if available)
  in this environment; actual cluster apply + a documented runbook is your
  verification step (I can't reach your cluster). Small app changes included and
  flagged: Dockerfile CMD ‚Üí uvicorn-only, and adding the ingress host to the
  CORS allowlist.

  Does this look right? If so I'll write it up as the spec.

‚óŹ Update(~/Documents/Shared/projects/docextractor/docs/superpowers/specs/2026-06
        -18-k8s-deployment-design.md)
  ‚éŅ ¬†Added 15 lines, removed 1 line
       79  
       80  ## Migrations
       81  
       82 -`migrate-job.yaml` ‚ÄĒ a Job annotated `helm.sh/hook: pre-instal
          -l,pre-upgrade` + `hook-weight` + `hook-delete-policy: before-h
          -ook-creation,hook-succeeded`. Uses the backend image, the same
          - env (needs `DOCEXTRACTOR_DATABASE_URL_SYNC`), command `alembi
          -c upgrade head`. Ensures exactly one migration run per deploy 
          -before the app pods roll. Backend Dockerfile `CMD` is changed 
          -to uvicorn-only.                                              
       82 +> **Amended during implementation.** The original plan used a 
          +Helm `pre-install,pre-upgrade` hook                           
       83 +> Job. That fails a *fresh* install: hook resources run before
          + non-hook resources, so the migrate                           
       84 +> Job runs before the (non-hook) Postgres StatefulSet exists a
          +nd aborts the install. Rather than make                       
       85 +> Postgres a hook (which breaks upgrade/uninstall lifecycle), 
          +migrations moved into a backend pod                           
       86 +> **init container**.                                         
       87  
       88 +The backend Deployment has an init container `migrate` (backen
          +d image, same `envFrom` config+secret,                        
       89 +command `alembic upgrade head`) that runs before the `backend`
          + container. If Postgres is not yet                            
       90 +reachable the init container exits non-zero and the kubelet re
          +tries it with backoff until Postgres is                       
       91 +ready ‚ÄĒ so no Helm hook ordering or explicit wait loop is need
          +ed, on either install or upgrade. The                         
       92 +app's startup `create_all()` is a no-op once Alembic has built
          + the schema (`checkfirst`). The worker                        
       93 +and scheduler Deployments get a `wait-for-backend` init contai
          +ner (HTTP-polls the backend                                   
       94 +`/api/health`) so they only start once the schema exists. With
          + no hook resources left, the ConfigMap                        
       95 +and Secret are plain release resources (cleaned up on `helm un
          +install`). Backend Dockerfile `CMD` is                        
       96 +uvicorn-only.                                                 
       97 +                                                              
       98  ## Images & CI
       99  
      100  `.github/workflows/images.yml`: on push to `main` and on `v*` 
           tags, build+push `ghcr.io/carev01/doc-extractor-backend` (cont
           ext `backend/`) and `-frontend` (context `frontend/`, build-ar
           g `VITE_API_BASE_URL=""`) via `docker/build-push-action`, tagg
           ed with the git SHA and `latest` (and the version tag when tag
           ged). Uses `GITHUB_TOKEN` with `packages: write`. Chart `value
           s.image.{backend,frontend}.{repository,tag,pullPolicy}` defaul
           t to these; `imagePullSecret` values block included but defaul
           t-empty (public packages).

  - Endpoint reachable from inside the cluster ‚ÄĒ a live call from the backend
  pod returned HTTP 200.
  - Response shape is compatible ‚ÄĒ the app reads choices[0].message.content, and
  a realistic call returned clean {"ok": true} JSON there. The endpoint also
  honored the response_format: json_object the app sends. (gpt-oss-20b is a
  reasoning model ‚ÄĒ it puts its thinking in a separate reasoning_content field,
  which is why a 5-token test came back with empty content; at the app's
  512-token budget it emits content fine.)

  The LLM fallback now triggers automatically when extraction hits a
  documentation site that none of the built-in profiles recognize ‚ÄĒ it derives a
  selector spec from the page and caches it to
  source.profile_config["llm_spec"] so future runs skip the LLM call.

  One thing worth flagging: the app hardcodes max_tokens: 512 for the derivation
  call (backend/app/services/profiles/llm.py). For a reasoning model that
  spends tokens thinking before emitting the JSON spec, that can occasionally be
  tight on a large/complex TOC page. It worked in testing, but if you ever see
  the LLM fallback return no spec for a complex site, that ceiling is the first
  thing to raise. Want me to bump it (it'd need a code change + image rebuild,
  or making it a configurable setting)?

‚óŹ The smoking gun is in the events:

  Liveness probe failed: sh: 1: pgrep: not found

  Root cause: a bug in my Helm chart. The worker and scheduler liveness probes
  run pgrep -f 'app.worker', but pgrep (the procps package) isn't installed in 
  the Python slim image. So the liveness probe fails every cycle, and the
  kubelet SIGKILLs the container (exit 137) ~2 minutes after each start. The
  node has plenty of memory (34% used) ‚ÄĒ it's not OOM. The scheduler is
  crash-looping for the same reason (you saw RESTARTS 5 earlier).

  That's why the extraction dies at ~4 pages: the worker gets ~2 minutes of
  scraping in, gets killed mid-run, restarts, and the run is left as a RUNNING
  zombie that nothing resumes.

  Ran 1 shell command (ctrl+o to expand)

  What was wrong (and it was my bug)

  Helm chart I wrote:

  - The worker and scheduler liveness probes ran pgrep -f 'app.worker', but the

  cycle, so the kubelet SIGKILLed both containers (~exit¬†137) roughly every 2 
  minutes.
  - Result: the worker got ~2 minutes of scraping in (your first ~4 pages), got
  killed mid-run, and the extraction was left as a RUNNING zombie with a frozen
  heartbeat. The scheduler, which runs the stale-run reaper that would normally
  recover such runs, was crash-looping for the exact same reason ‚ÄĒ so nothing
  recovered it. It wasn't slow; it was dead after 4 pages.
  - It was not OOM (node was at 34% memory) and not Firecrawl (reachable in
  0.03s).

‚óŹ process_article_result is called with change_status. My forming hypothesis:
  when Firecrawl reports changeStatus: "same", our code skips persisting ‚ÄĒ

‚óŹ Root cause confirmed. Look at lines 350‚Äď371: when change_status == "same", the
  code does a blind UPDATE Article ... WHERE source_url = url and returns
  "unchanged" ‚ÄĒ it never checks whether the UPDATE matched any row. The
  docstring (337‚Äď341) states the buggy assumption explicitly: "When 'same', the 
  DB write is skipped entirely." It assumes Firecrawl's "same" verdict means our
  DB already has the article.

  That assumption was violated by the crash-loop: the killed attempts scraped
  pages into Firecrawl's changeTracking baseline (keyed by the shared tag: 
  src-{source_id}) but died before persisting to our DB. So on the final
  successful run, Firecrawl says "same" for all 88 sub-pages, the UPDATE matches
  zero rows, and they're silently dropped. Only the 4 root-anchor articles (all
  mapping to /docs/, which got persisted as "new" early) survived ‚ÄĒ which is
  exactly why the UI shows one page and TOC clicks hit nothing.

‚óŹ Done. Here's the full picture.

  Root cause (systematic-debugging)

  The symptoms ‚ÄĒ one visible article, dead TOC clicks ‚ÄĒ traced to one backend 
  bug, surfaced by the earlier crash-loop:

  In process_article_result, the change_status == "same" fast-path did a blind 
  UPDATE ... WHERE source_url = url and returned "unchanged" without checking 
  whether any row matched. The docstring literally encoded the wrong assumption:
  "When 'same', the DB write is skipped entirely."

  Firecrawl's changeTracking baseline is keyed by a shared per-source tag. The
  crash-looping worker scraped pages (seeding that baseline) but was SIGKILLed
  before persisting them to our DB. So the final run got "same" for 88 pages our
  DB never had ‚ÄĒ and the blind UPDATE silently dropped them. Only the 4
  root-anchor articles (which mapped to /docs/ and persisted as "new") survived.
  Hence 92 TOC entries, 4 articles, identical content.

  I proved it with evidence before touching anything: detection was correct (it
  is mkdocs Material), Firecrawl returned correctly distinct content per URL
  (athena = 15,787 bytes), so the fault was ours, in the batch-result
  persistence path.

  The fix (659aa67, on main, deployed)

  The "same" branch now short-circuits only when the UPDATE matches a row;
  otherwise it falls through and persists the content scraped this run. Added a
  regression test (test_same_status_persists_when_article_missing) ‚ÄĒ it failed
  before the fix, passes after, and all 22 test_versions.py tests pass (run
  against a port-forwarded cluster Postgres).

  Verified on the live cluster

  - Re-extraction climbed 4 ‚Üí 90 articles and COMPLETED.
  - 90 articles, 80 distinct content hashes, sizes 391‚Äď20,642 bytes (no more
  identical blob); AWS Athena = 15,787 bytes, exactly matching the direct
  Firecrawl scrape.
  - 90/90 articles linked to a TOC entry; the API serves the full 92-node TOC + 
  90 articles. (The 2 unstored entries are off-domain
  app.satoricyber.com/docs/api and a registry.terraform.io link that return
  empty content ‚ÄĒ correctly skipped.)
  - All 5 pods healthy, 0 restarts.

‚óŹ Done ‚ÄĒ fixed, deployed (revision 6), and verified end-to-end.

  Root cause (it was both layers, as you suspected on the frontend)

  You were right that the frontend was misbehaving, but there were two coupled
  defects:

  1. Backend (exporter.py): _generate_export unconditionally built a ZIP for
  every export. A PDF is already self-contained (images embedded), so a PDF
  export wrote both Satori.pdf (46 MB) and a redundant Satori.zip (41 MB) that
  just re-wrapped the same PDF.
  2. Frontend (ExportPanel.tsx): it always rendered a primary button hardcoded
  "Download ZIP (markdown + images)" ‚ÄĒ even for PDF ‚ÄĒ so the download looked
  like an unrequested markdown bundle. (Plus the per-file endpoint served .pdf
  as text/markdown.)

  I verified this against your actual export on disk before changing anything:
  the old PDF export (7de77158) genuinely had Satori.pdf + Satori.zip, and the
  ZIP contained only the PDF.

  The fix

  - Backend: no ZIP for format == "pdf" (zip_filename is now null);
  ExportResponse.zip_filename is optional; the per-file download serves
  application/pdf for .pdf.
  - Frontend: the ZIP button only renders when a ZIP actually exists (markdown
  exports); for PDF the .pdf link becomes the primary download.
  - Tests: new test_export_format (PDF ‚Üí no zip, markdown ‚Üí zip, run with a
  mocked renderer), and updated test_export_worker which had been asserting the
  buggy behavior (a zip for a PDF export).

  Verified live

  A fresh PDF export (2ff735f3) now produces only Satori.pdf ‚ÄĒ no ZIP ‚ÄĒ the API
  returns zip_filename: null, the download is content-type: application/pdf, and
  the ZIP endpoint correctly 404s. Markdown exports still bundle .md + images
  into a ZIP as before. All pods healthy on sha-5454edb, 0 restarts.

  One note: your earlier PDF export still has its redundant ZIP sitting on disk
  (past artifact ‚ÄĒ not regenerated). A fresh export gives you the clean PDF-only
  result. Hard-refresh the browser to pick up the new frontend.

‚óŹ Let me confirm the frontend doesn't already surface past exports, and check

‚óŹ Confirmed both answers. Here's what's actually happening, then the plan.

  Answers to your questions

  1. Export files stay forever ‚ÄĒ there is no cleanup at all. I grepped the whole
  backend: zero retention/purge/TTL logic. Every export directory (PDF, ZIP,
  markdown, images) accumulates on the exports PVC indefinitely. Right now that
  PVC is 4.9 Gi, 3% used (128 MB across 3 exports) ‚ÄĒ but at ~46 MB per PDF
  export it would fill after ~100 exports, and once full, new exports fail with 
  disk-full errors. So this is a real operational time-bomb, not just
  untidiness.

  2. The file is NOT deleted ‚ÄĒ you just lose access to it in the UI. The
  ExportPanel keeps the result in React local state; navigating away unmounts
  the component and the download link vanishes. The files are still on disk.
  There's even an /api/export/list endpoint that enumerates past exports ‚ÄĒ but
  the frontend never calls it, so there's no "past exports" view. So today:
  files pile up forever and you can't get back to them. Worst of both.

  Now let me write the plan into a backlog file:

‚óŹ Done. The backlog item is implemented, deployed, and verified.

  What I built (Phases 1 & 2)

  Phase 1 ‚ÄĒ Retention sweep (the disk time-bomb):
  - New purge_expired_exports runs in the scheduler (hourly, gated so it doesn't
  walk the volume every 30s tick). It deletes export directories and their
  export_jobs rows once older than DOCEXTRACTOR_EXPORT_RETENTION_DAYS (default
  7), and evicts oldest-first if the total footprint exceeds
  DOCEXTRACTOR_EXPORT_MAX_TOTAL_BYTES (default 3 GiB). Orphan dirs past the
  cutoff are swept too. Both knobs are exposed in the Helm chart.
  - Tested: age sweep, size-cap eviction, idempotency / missing-dir tolerance (3
  tests, all green against a real Postgres).

  Phase 2 ‚ÄĒ Persistent access (the "link disappears" problem):
  - /api/export/list now reads from export_jobs (joined to the source) and
  returns rich metadata ‚ÄĒ source, format, created/expires timestamps, files,
  zip, size ‚ÄĒ newest first, skipping anything already purged.
  - The Export page loads this on mount and after each export, so a "Recent 
  Exports" list with working download links now survives navigating away and
  back.

  Verified live (revision 8, docextractor namespace)

  - /api/export/list returns both Satori PDF exports with full metadata and
  expires_at = created + 7 days; the newer one correctly shows zip_filename: 
  null, the older (pre-zip-fix) one shows its .zip.
  - Scheduler healthy, 0 restarts, first purge tick ran clean (nothing to purge
  yet ‚ÄĒ exports are recent and 128 MB ‚Č™ 3 GiB cap).
  - Backend tests: 8 export-related tests pass. Frontend type-checks/builds.
  - Caught and fixed a latent crash en route: the 3 GiB value first rendered as
  "3.2e+09" (Helm float-ifies large ints), which pydantic can't parse as int ‚ÄĒ
  quoting it in values keeps it a literal integer string.

  Answers to your original questions, now resolved

  - "Do they stay forever?" They did ‚ÄĒ now they're auto-purged after 7 days (and
  capped at 3 GiB) so the PVC can't fill.
  - "Was the file deleted when the link vanished?" No, it was just lost UI state
  ‚ÄĒ now the Export page lists your recent exports persistently with download
  links, and shows when each expires.

  Hard-refresh the browser to pick up the new frontend and the "Recent Exports"
  section.

  Backlog (docs/BACKLOG.md) is updated: Phases 1 & 2 marked done; Phase 3 
  remains as a stretch ‚ÄĒ a manual "delete export now" button and moving export
  artifacts to object storage (which would also unblock scaling backend/worker
  past one node).

  One operational note: the retention values are now in the chart's ConfigMap,
  but app pods read env at startup, so if you change
  export.retentionDays/maxTotalBytes later you'll need a kubectl rollout restart
  for it to take effect (same as the other settings ‚ÄĒ there's no
  config-checksum auto-restart on the deployments).

‚óŹ The format is clear: the master TOC defines the tree ({i, c, n} nodes = index,
  chunk, children) and names chunk files (OnlineMasterTOC_Chunk0.js,
  numchunks:1) that hold the actual entries. Let me inspect a chunk to see the
  title/href format:

  Ran 1 shell command (ctrl+o to expand)

‚óŹ Now I have the complete Flare TOC format:
  - Master TOC (OnlineMasterTOC.js): tree of {i, c, n} nodes (index, chunk,
  children ‚ÄĒ pure numbers) + numchunks/prefix.
  - Chunk (..._Chunk0.js): define({'<href>':{i:[idx], t:['<title>'], b:['']}, 
  ...}) ‚ÄĒ maps href‚Üíindex+title.

  So the robust, general fix: fetch Data/HelpSystem.xml ‚Üí read Toc= ‚Üí fetch the
  master TOC + chunks ‚Üí resolve the tree into an ordered, hierarchical TOC. Let
  me look at the Scraper interface, strategies, and detector to wire this in
  correctly:

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

‚óŹ The Scraper only does Firecrawl HTML fetches ‚ÄĒ I'll need a raw-GET capability

      229 +    async def fetch_raw(self, url: str) -> str:               
      230 +        """Plain GET of a static asset, bypassing Firecrawl's 
          +HTML cleaning.                                                
      231 +                                                              
      232 +        Used for non-HTML resources a profile needs verbatim ‚ÄĒ
          + e.g. MadCap Flare's                                          
      233 +        ``Data/*.xml``/``Data/Tocs/*.js`` TOC files, which Fir
          +ecrawl would strip or                                         
      234 +        mangle. Sends a browser UA; raises on HTTP error.     
      235 +        """                                                   
      236 +        resp = await self.client.get(                         
      237 +            url, headers={"User-Agent": _BROWSER_UA}, follow_r
          +edirects=True                                                 
      238 +        )                                                     
      239 +        resp.raise_for_status()                               
      240 +        return resp.text

  ‚éŅ ¬†Added 125 lines
      130      return out
      131  
      132  
      133 +async def _try_get_raw(scraper, url: str) -> str | None:      
      134 +    """Best-effort verbatim GET; None on any error (incl. 404)
          +."""                                                          
      135 +    try:                                                      
      136 +        txt = await scraper.get_raw(url)                      
      137 +        return txt or None                                    
      138 +    except Exception:                                         
      139 +        return None                                           
      140 +                                                              
      141 +                                                              
      142 +def _js_unescape(s: str) -> str:                              
      143 +    return s.replace("\\'", "'").replace('\\"', '"').replace("
          +\\\\", "\\")                                                  
      144 +                                                              
      145 +                                                              
      146 +def _parse_flare_tree(master: str) -> dict | None:            
      147 +    """Extract the numeric ``tree:{...}`` object from a Flare 
          +master TOC.                                                   
      148 +                                                              
      149 +    The tree holds only integers and the keys i/c/n (no string
          +s), so it can be                                              
      150 +    safely JSON-ified by quoting those keys.                  
      151 +    """                                                       
      152 +    i = master.find("tree:")                                  
      153 +    if i == -1:                                               
      154 +        return None                                           
      155 +    j = master.find("{", i)                                   
      156 +    if j == -1:                                               
      157 +        return None                                           
      158 +    depth = 0                                                 
      159 +    blob = None                                               
      160 +    for k in range(j, len(master)):                           
      161 +        if master[k] == "{":                                  
      162 +            depth += 1                                        
      163 +        elif master[k] == "}":                                
      164 +            depth -= 1                                        
      165 +            if depth == 0:                                    
      166 +                blob = master[j:k + 1]                        
      167 +                break                                         
      168 +    if blob is None:                                          
      169 +        return None                                           
      170 +    jsonish = re.sub(r'([{,\[])\s*([icn])\s*:', r'\1"\2":', bl
          +ob)                                                           
      171 +    try:                                                      
      172 +        return json.loads(jsonish)                            
      173 +    except (ValueError, TypeError):                           
      174 +        return None                                           
      175 +                                                              
      176 +                                                              
      177 +def _parse_flare_chunk(text: str) -> dict[int, tuple[str, str]
          +]:                                                            
      178 +    """Parse a Flare TOC chunk: ``'<href>':{i:[idx,...],t:['<t
          +itle>'],...}``.                                               
      179 +                                                              
      180 +    Returns {tree_index: (href, title)}.                      
      181 +    """                                                       
      182 +    out: dict[int, tuple[str, str]] = {}                      
      183 +    pat = re.compile(                                         
      184 +        r"'((?:[^'\\]|\\.)*)'\s*:\s*\{i:\[([\d,\s]+)\]\s*,\s*t
          +:\['((?:[^'\\]|\\.)*)'\]"                                     
      185 +    )                                                         
      186 +    for m in pat.finditer(text):                              
      187 +        href = _js_unescape(m.group(1))                       
      188 +        title = _js_unescape(m.group(3))                      
      189 +        for idx in m.group(2).split(","):                     
      190 +            idx = idx.strip()                                 
      191 +            if idx.isdigit():                                 
      192 +                out[int(idx)] = (href, title)                 
      193 +    return out                                                
      194 +                                                              
      195 +                                                              
      196 +async def flare_helpsystem_toc(scraper, root_url: str) -> list
          +[TocEntry]:                                                   
      197 +    """Build a MadCap Flare TOC from its static ``Data/`` file
          +s.                                                            
      198 +                                                              
      199 +    Flare renders the TOC client-side from data files (``Data/
          +HelpSystem.xml``                                              
      200 +    names the TOC; the master TOC defines the tree and referen
          +ces chunk files                                               
      201 +    holding each entry's href+title), so the TOC never appears
          + in the page HTML.                                            
      202 +    We fetch and resolve those files into an ordered, hierarch
          +ical TOC.                                                     
      203 +                                                              
      204 +    Returns [] when the data files aren't web-served (older/se
          +rver-side Flare                                               
      205 +    outputs), so callers can fall back to parsing the rendered
          + nav.                                                         
      206 +    """                                                       
      207 +    # Help-system root = parent of the Content/ directory hold
          +ing the topic.                                                
      208 +    help_root = urljoin(root_url, "../")                      
      209 +    hs_xml = await _try_get_raw(scraper, urljoin(help_root, "D
          +ata/HelpSystem.xml"))                                         
      210 +    if not hs_xml:                                            
      211 +        return []                                             
      212 +    m = re.search(r'\bToc="([^"]+)"', hs_xml)                 
      213 +    if not m:                                                 
      214 +        return []                                             
      215 +    master_url = urljoin(help_root, m.group(1))               
      216 +    master = await _try_get_raw(scraper, master_url)          
      217 +    if not master:                                            
      218 +        return []                                             
      219 +                                                              
      220 +    tree = _parse_flare_tree(master)                          
      221 +    prefix_m = re.search(r"prefix:'([^']*)'", master)         
      222 +    if tree is None or not prefix_m:                          
      223 +        return []                                             
      224 +    prefix = prefix_m.group(1)                                
      225 +    numchunks_m = re.search(r"numchunks:(\d+)", master)       
      226 +    numchunks = int(numchunks_m.group(1)) if numchunks_m else 
          +1                                                             
      227 +                                                              
      228 +    chunks: dict[int, dict[int, tuple[str, str]]] = {}        
      229 +    for c in range(numchunks):                                
      230 +        txt = await _try_get_raw(scraper, urljoin(master_url, 
          +f"{prefix}{c}.js"))                                           
      231 +        chunks[c] = _parse_flare_chunk(txt) if txt else {}    
      232 +                                                              
      233 +    out: list[TocEntry] = []                                  
      234 +                                                              
      235 +    def walk(nodes: list, level: int, parent_url: str | None) 
          +-> None:                                                      
      236 +        for node in nodes:                                    
      237 +            idx = node.get("i")                               
      238 +            entry = chunks.get(node.get("c", 0), {}).get(idx) 
      239 +            kids = node.get("n")                              
      240 +            if entry is None:                                 
      241 +                # Container with no resolvable entry: descend,
          + keep the parent.                                             
      242 +                if kids:                                      
      243 +                    walk(kids, level, parent_url)             
      244 +                continue                                      
      245 +            href, title = entry                               
      246 +            url = urljoin(help_root, href.lstrip("/"))        
      247 +            out.append(TocEntry(                              
      248 +                title=title, url=url, level=level,            
      249 +                is_article=not kids, parent_url=parent_url,   
      250 +            ))                                                
      251 +            if kids:                                          
      252 +                walk(kids, level + 1, url)                    
      253 +                                                              
      254 +    walk(tree.get("n", []), 0, None)                          
      255 +    return out                                                
      256 +                                                              
      257 +                                                              
      258  async def sitemap_urls(scraper, root_url: str) -> list[str]:
      259      """Return all <loc> URLs from the site's sitemap.xml, in d
           ocument order."""
      260      parsed = urlparse(root_url)

‚óŹ Done ‚ÄĒ fully fixed and verified. The title now reads "What is Datto's new and 
  improved infrastructure..." (the \u0027 is decoded), and the run COMPLETED.

  Root cause (systematic-debugging)

  MadCap Flare HTML5/WebHelp (which is what the Datto bookshelf is) renders its
  TOC entirely client-side from static Data/ files ‚ÄĒ the <ul class="sidenav"> in
  the page HTML is empty, and Firecrawl doesn't run Flare's TOC loader. So:
  - The auto-detected flare_html5 profile parsed the empty sidenav ‚Üí 1 page (the
  home topic).
  - The LLM fallback scraped the ~7 link tiles in the home page body ‚Üí not the
  TOC.

  I traced the real TOC to Data/HelpSystem.xml ‚Üí
  Toc="Data/Tocs/OnlineMasterTOC.js" ‚Üí a tree of {i,c,n} nodes + chunk files
  holding each entry's href/title.

  Three fixes (each tested, committed, deployed)

  1. flare_helpsystem_toc (3a105e7) ‚ÄĒ fetches HelpSystem.xml, reads the TOC
  file, parses the master tree + chunks into an ordered, hierarchical TOC. Both
  Flare profiles try this first and fall back to the rendered nav when the data
  files aren't web-served. Added Scraper.get_raw/FirecrawlService.fetch_raw for
  verbatim asset fetches.
  2. Per-page resilience (3001e29) ‚ÄĒ a single page's Firecrawl 500 was aborting
  the whole run (it failed at 49/119 the first time). Per-page processing is now
  wrapped so a bad page is logged and skipped; the run completes best-effort.
  3. \uXXXX title decoding (7830f0a) ‚ÄĒ Flare encodes apostrophes etc. as \u0027;
  the unescaper now decodes them.

  Verified live (revision 11)

  - Auto-detected flare_html5; built 119 TOC entries (was¬†1), depth 3, correct
  hierarchy.
  - Extraction COMPLETED: 118 articles, 118 distinct content hashes (no
  repeated-blob issue), all TOC-linked, content 1‚Äď63 KB. The 1 unscraped entry
  is a page Firecrawl 500s on ‚ÄĒ correctly skipped instead of failing the run.

  Hard-refresh the browser and you'll see the full Datto TOC with all topics
  navigable.

  A note on process, per your earlier point: I treated this as "troubleshoot and
  fix now" since you explicitly asked me to fix it. The export-lifecycle item
  from before remains the model for "add to backlog" = queue for later.
